CHAPTER ______
1 AN ACT concerning
2 Creation of a State Debt – Maryland Consolidated Capital Bond Loan of 2026,
3 and the Maryland Consolidated Capital Bond Loans of 2015, 2016, 2017, 2018,
4 2019, 2020, 2021, 2022, 2023, 2024, and 2025
5 FOR the purpose of authorizing the creation of a State Debt in the amount of One Billion,
6 Eight Hundred and Twenty–Four Million, Seven Hundred and Eighty–Two
7 Thousand Dollars ($1,824,782,000) One Billion, Seven Hundred and Fifty–Eight
8 Million, Two Hundred and Sixty–One Thousand, Nine Hundred and Six Dollars
9 ($1,758,261,906), the proceeds to be used for certain necessary building,
10 construction, demolition, planning, renovation, conversion, replacement, and capital
11 equipment purchases of the State, for acquiring certain real estate in connection
12 therewith, and for grants to certain subdivisions and other organizations for certain
13 development and improvement purposes; subject to certain requirements that
14 certain matching funds be provided and expended by certain dates; providing
15 generally for the issuance and sale of bonds evidencing the loan; imposing a certain
16 tax on all assessable property in the State; specifying the use of certain school
17 construction funds; removing certain matching fund requirements; requiring that
18 certain grantees convey certain easements under certain circumstances to the
19 Maryland Historical Trust; providing that the proceeds of certain loans must be
20 expended or encumbered by a certain date; providing that certain funds may be used
21 only for certain purposes; requiring the Department of General Services to record
22 certain correct information in certain grant agreements under certain
23 circumstances, notwithstanding certain differences; authorizing the Board of Public
24 Works, under certain circumstances, to approve certain appropriations,
25 notwithstanding certain differences; authorizing certain unexpended appropriations
EXPLANATION: CAPITALS INDICATE MATTER ADDED TO EXISTING LAW.
[Brackets] indicate matter deleted from existing law.
Underlining indicates amendments to bill.
Strike out indicates matter stricken from the bill by amendment or deleted from the law by
amendment. *sb0283*
2 SENATE BILL 283
1 in certain prior capital budgets and bond loans to be expended for other public
2 projects; altering certain requirements for certain programs in certain prior capital
3 budgets and bond loans; reducing prior authorizations of State Debt; requiring that
4 certain projects be constructed at certain locations; adding, altering, and repealing
5 certain requirements for certain appropriations; altering and expanding the
6 authorized purpose of certain grants; providing that certain grants may not
7 terminate before certain dates; authorizing premiums from the sale of State bonds
8 in certain fiscal years to be used for certain purposes; requiring the Comptroller to
9 make certain transfers, adjustments, and reconciliations; repealing certain
10 Maryland Consolidated Capital Bond Loan Preauthorization acts; specifying the use
11 of certain project funds; authorizing the creation of State Debt in certain years to be
12 used for certain purposes; clarifying the use of certain bond proceeds; and generally
13 relating to the financing of certain capital projects.

6 Section 13, 14, 15, and 16
7 SECTION 1. BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF MARYLAND,
8 That:
9 (1) The Board of Public Works may borrow money and incur indebtedness on
10 behalf of the State of Maryland through a State loan to be known as the Maryland
11 Consolidated Capital Bond Loan of 2026 in the total principal amount of $1,824,782,000
12 $1,758,261,906. This loan shall be evidenced by the issuance, sale, and delivery of State
13 general obligation bonds authorized by a resolution of the Board of Public Works and
14 issued, sold, and delivered in accordance with §§ 8–117 through 8–124 and 8–131.2 of the
15 State Finance and Procurement Article.
16 (2) The bonds to evidence this loan or installments of this loan may be sold as a
17 single issue of bonds under § 8–122 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.
18 (3) The cash proceeds of the sale of the bonds shall be paid to the Treasurer and
19 first shall be applied to the payment of the expenses of issuing, selling, and delivering the
20 bonds, unless funds for this purpose are otherwise provided, and then shall be credited on
21 the books of the Comptroller and expended on approval by the Board of Public Works, for
22 the following public purposes, including any applicable architects’ and engineers’ fees:
23 EXECUTIVE DEPARTMENT – GOVERNOR

9 Provided that grants may be provided only to nonpublic schools

11 purchase of textbooks or computer hardware and software for
12 loans to students in eligible nonpublic schools) during the
13 2025–2026 school year or nonpublic schools that serve students
14 with disabilities through the Non–Public Placement Program
15 R00A02.07 Subprogram 0762, excluding preschools in fiscal
16 2027, with a maximum amount of $100,000 and a minimum
17 amount of $5,000 per eligible school.
18 Further provided that:
19 (a) Unless a school serves students through the
20 Non–Public Placement Program, an eligible school
21 may apply and qualify for a grant as specified below
22 based on the following criteria:
23 (1) At least 20% of the school’s
24 students are eligible for free
25 or reduced price meal
26 programs;
27 (2) Tuition charged to students
28 is less than the statewide
29 average per pupil
30 expenditure for public
31 schools as calculated by the
32 Maryland State Department
33 of Education; and
34 (3) The school has a facility with
35 an average age of 50 years or
36 more; and
37 (b) If a school meets:
38 (1) All three of the criteria
39 specified above, the school

1 may receive up to $100,000;
2 (2) Two of the three criteria
3 specified above, the school
4 may receive up to $75,000;
5 and
6 (3) One of the three criteria
7 specified above, the school
8 may receive up to $25,000.
9 Further provided that if more eligible schools apply and qualify
10 for grants than the total authorizations, the Maryland State
11 Department of Education shall prorate the grants based on the

17 (5) (a) Prior to the payment of any matching grant funds under the provisions
18 of Section 1(3) Items ZA00 through ZB02 of this Act, grantees shall provide and expend
19 matching funds as specified. No part of a grantee’s matching fund may be provided, either
20 directly or indirectly, from funds of the State, whether appropriated or unappropriated.
21 Except as otherwise provided, no part of the fund may consist of real property, in kind
22 contributions, or funds expended prior to the effective date of this Act. In case of any dispute
23 as to what money or assets may qualify as matching funds, the Board of Public Works shall
24 determine the matter, and the Board’s decision is final. Grantees have until June 1, 2028,
25 to present evidence satisfactory to the Board of Public Works that the matching fund will
26 be provided. If satisfactory evidence is presented, the Board shall certify this fact to the
27 State Treasurer and the proceeds of the loan shall be expended for the purposes provided in
28 this Act. If this evidence is not presented by June 1, 2028, the proceeds of the loan shall be
29 applied to the purposes authorized in § 8–129 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.
30 (b) It is further provided that when an equal and matching fund is specified
31 in Section 1(3) Items ZA00 through ZB02 of this Act, grantees shall provide a matching fund
32 equal to the lesser of (i) the authorized amount of the State grant or (ii) the amount of the
33 matching fund certified by the Board of Public Works. If satisfactory evidence is presented,
34 the Board shall certify this fact and the amount of the matching fund to the State Treasurer
35 and the proceeds of the loan equal to the amount of the matching fund shall be expended for
36 the purposes provided in this Act. If this evidence is not presented by June 1, 2028, the
37 proceeds of the loan shall be applied to the purposes authorized in § 8–129 of the State
38 Finance and Procurement Article. The proceeds of any amount of the loan in excess of the
39 matching fund certified by the Board of Public Works shall also be applied to the purposes
40 authorized in § 8–129 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.

1 (6) (a) Prior to approval by the Board of Public Works of an expenditure of bond

4 on the property where the capital project assisted by the bond proceeds is located if the
5 Director of the Trust determines that the capital project impacts real property that is

22 writing to the Board of Public Works that the proposed use of funds may be approved
23 notwithstanding technical differences in the appropriation in Section 1(3) Items ZA00
24 through ZB02 of this Act.

12 SECTION 3. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That the General Assembly
13 declares that it is the public policy of this State to manage State general obligation bond
14 debt in a manner that will maintain Maryland’s high quality credit rating. The General
15 Assembly further declares that legislative oversight, control, and review of all forms of
16 State obligations are essential to maintenance of the State’s existing bond rating and
17 protection of the fiscal integrity of the State.
18 SECTION 4. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, before work may commence
19 pursuant to any supplement to any appropriation contained in this Act, satisfactory
20 evidence must be given to the Board of Public Works that the project can be completed with
21 the aggregate of the funds in this Act and previously appropriated for the stated purpose.
22 SECTION 5. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
23 (1) with the approval of the Department of Budget and Management, any
24 appropriation for design provided in this Act may be used to fund construction if the amount
25 of the appropriation exceeds the amount required for design expenses, including allowances
26 for contingencies; and
27 (2) with the approval of the Department of Budget and Management, any
28 appropriation for construction provided in this Act may be used to purchase capital
29 equipment if the amount of the appropriation exceeds the amount required for construction
30 expenses, including allowances for contingencies.
31 SECTION 6. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, except as otherwise provided
32 in this Act, before a State agency or institution named in this Act as responsible for an
33 individual item may begin work with funds appropriated by this Act, the agency or
34 institution shall provide satisfactory evidence to the Board of Public Works that the work
35 described in the individual item can be completed with the funds specified for that item.
36 SECTION 7. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, with the approval of the
37 Department of Budget and Management, any appropriation under the provisions of this
38 Act that is in excess of the amount needed for a project may be credited to the Construction
39 Contingency Fund under § 3–609 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.
120 SENATE BILL 283
1 Notwithstanding the fund balance restriction set forth in § 3–609(c) of the State Finance
2 and Procurement Article, any funds credited to the Fund may cause the total balance in
3 the Fund to exceed 1.25% of the capital debt affordability limit as determined under Title
4 8 of the State Finance and Procurement Article, in fiscal year 2027.
5 SECTION 8. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, if federal funds are available
6 to help accomplish any project identified in this Act, the State agency or institution
7 responsible for the project shall make efforts through proper administrative procedures to
8 obtain these federal funds. Before spending any funds appropriated by this Act, the agency
9 or institution shall certify its efforts to the Board of Public Works and state the reason for
10 any failure to obtain federal funds. If federal funds are obtained, they shall be used to defray
11 the costs of the project described in this Act and not to expand its scope.
12 SECTION 9. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
13 (1) for any appropriation for the planning of a State–owned project provided in
14 this Act, if a program required by § 3–602(d) of the State Finance and Procurement Article
15 has not been submitted, the State agency or institution responsible for the project shall
16 submit a program to the Department of Budget and Management for approval before funds
17 may be expended from the appropriation; and
18 (2) for any appropriation for the construction of a State–owned project provided
19 in this Act, if preliminary plans and outline specifications required by § 3–602(f)(2)(i) of the
20 State Finance and Procurement Article have not been prepared, the State agency or
21 institution responsible for the project shall submit preliminary plans and outline
22 specifications to the Department of Budget and Management for approval before funds may
23 be expended from the appropriation.
24 SECTION 10. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That no portion of the proceeds of
25 a loan or any of the matching funds provided for a project funded under this Act may be
26 used for the furtherance of an essentially religious endeavor. Upon the request of the Board
27 of Public Works, a recipient of the proceeds of a loan under this Act shall submit evidence
28 satisfactory to the Board that none of the proceeds of the loan or any matching funds have
29 been or are being used for a purpose prohibited by this Act.
30 SECTION 11. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That the Comptroller may
31 advance funds to any loan funds account established pursuant to a general obligation bond
32 loan enabling Act for any expenditure authorized by that Act, provided that if general
33 obligation bonds have not been issued under the authority of that Act, the next ensuing
34 sale of general obligation bonds shall include the issuance of bonds under the authority of
35 that Act in an amount at least equivalent to the amount of the funds so advanced.
36 SECTION 12. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That Section(s) 13, 14, 15, and 16
37 of Chapter 603 of the Acts of the General Assembly of 2025 be repealed.

CHAPTER ______
1 AN ACT concerning
2 Creation of a State Debt – Maryland Consolidated Capital Bond Loan of 2026,
3 and the Maryland Consolidated Capital Bond Loans of 2015, 2016, 2017, 2018,
4 2019, 2020, 2021, 2022, 2023, 2024, and 2025
5 FOR the purpose of authorizing the creation of a State Debt in the amount of One Billion,
6 Eight Hundred and Twenty–Four Million, Seven Hundred and Eighty–Two
7 Thousand Dollars ($1,824,782,000) One Billion, Seven Hundred and Fifty–Eight
8 Million, Two Hundred and Sixty–One Thousand, Nine Hundred and Six Dollars
9 ($1,758,261,906), the proceeds to be used for certain necessary building,
10 construction, demolition, planning, renovation, conversion, replacement, and capital
11 equipment purchases of the State, for acquiring certain real estate in connection
12 therewith, and for grants to certain subdivisions and other organizations for certain
13 development and improvement purposes; subject to certain requirements that
14 certain matching funds be provided and expended by certain dates; providing
15 generally for the issuance and sale of bonds evidencing the loan; imposing a certain
16 tax on all assessable property in the State; specifying the use of certain school
17 construction funds; removing certain matching fund requirements; requiring that
18 certain grantees convey certain easements under certain circumstances to the
19 Maryland Historical Trust; providing that the proceeds of certain loans must be
20 expended or encumbered by a certain date; providing that certain funds may be used
21 only for certain purposes; requiring the Department of General Services to record
22 certain correct information in certain grant agreements under certain
23 circumstances, notwithstanding certain differences; authorizing the Board of Public
24 Works, under certain circumstances, to approve certain appropriations,
25 notwithstanding certain differences; authorizing certain unexpended appropriations

1 Chapter 603 of the Acts of the General Assembly of 2025
2 Section 1(1), (3) Item DE02.01(C) and (D), DH01.04(C), QB01.01(A), QT04(A),

4 BY repealing
5 Chapter 603 of the Acts of the General Assembly of 2025
6 Section 13, 14, 15, and 16
7 SECTION 1. BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF MARYLAND,
8 That:
9 (1) The Board of Public Works may borrow money and incur indebtedness on
10 behalf of the State of Maryland through a State loan to be known as the Maryland
11 Consolidated Capital Bond Loan of 2026 in the total principal amount of $1,824,782,000
12 $1,758,261,906. This loan shall be evidenced by the issuance, sale, and delivery of State
13 general obligation bonds authorized by a resolution of the Board of Public Works and
14 issued, sold, and delivered in accordance with §§ 8–117 through 8–124 and 8–131.2 of the
15 State Finance and Procurement Article.

13 (4) An annual tax is imposed on all assessable property in the State in rate and
14 amount sufficient to pay the principal of and interest on the bonds, as and when due and
15 until paid in full. The principal shall be discharged within 15 years after the date of issue
16 of the bonds.
17 (5) (a) Prior to the payment of any matching grant funds under the provisions
18 of Section 1(3) Items ZA00 through ZB02 of this Act, grantees shall provide and expend
19 matching funds as specified. No part of a grantee’s matching fund may be provided, either
20 directly or indirectly, from funds of the State, whether appropriated or unappropriated.
21 Except as otherwise provided, no part of the fund may consist of real property, in kind
22 contributions, or funds expended prior to the effective date of this Act. In case of any dispute
23 as to what money or assets may qualify as matching funds, the Board of Public Works shall
24 determine the matter, and the Board’s decision is final. Grantees have until June 1, 2028,
25 to present evidence satisfactory to the Board of Public Works that the matching fund will
26 be provided. If satisfactory evidence is presented, the Board shall certify this fact to the
27 State Treasurer and the proceeds of the loan shall be expended for the purposes provided in
28 this Act. If this evidence is not presented by June 1, 2028, the proceeds of the loan shall be
29 applied to the purposes authorized in § 8–129 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.
30 (b) It is further provided that when an equal and matching fund is specified
31 in Section 1(3) Items ZA00 through ZB02 of this Act, grantees shall provide a matching fund
32 equal to the lesser of (i) the authorized amount of the State grant or (ii) the amount of the
33 matching fund certified by the Board of Public Works. If satisfactory evidence is presented,
34 the Board shall certify this fact and the amount of the matching fund to the State Treasurer
35 and the proceeds of the loan equal to the amount of the matching fund shall be expended for
36 the purposes provided in this Act. If this evidence is not presented by June 1, 2028, the
37 proceeds of the loan shall be applied to the purposes authorized in § 8–129 of the State
38 Finance and Procurement Article. The proceeds of any amount of the loan in excess of the
39 matching fund certified by the Board of Public Works shall also be applied to the purposes
40 authorized in § 8–129 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.

1 (6) (a) Prior to approval by the Board of Public Works of an expenditure of bond
2 proceeds authorized under Section 1(3) Items ZA00 through ZB02 of this Act, the grantee
3 shall grant and convey to the Maryland Historical Trust a historic preservation easement
4 on the property where the capital project assisted by the bond proceeds is located if the
5 Director of the Trust determines that the capital project impacts real property that is
6 individually listed in, or eligible for individual listing in, the Maryland Register of Historic
7 Properties, unless the Director of the Trust also determines that the real property:
8 (i) Is a type that is already adequately represented among the
9 Trust’s existing easement properties;
10 (ii) Is already subject to adequate protections of historic preservation
11 law or instrument; or
12 (iii) Has conditions peculiar to it that make requiring an easement
13 impractical.
14 (b) If the grantee holds a lease on the property, the Trust may accept an
15 easement on the leasehold interest.
16 (c) The easement must be in form, substance, and duration acceptable to
17 the Director of the Trust.
18 (d) (i) A recipient may administratively appeal to the Maryland
19 Historical Trust Board of Trustees a determination made by the Director of the Trust under
20 subparagraph (a) of this paragraph.
21 (ii) The decision made by the Maryland Historical Trust Board of
22 Trustees on an appeal is final and is not subject to further administrative appeal or judicial
23 review.

26 authorized by this Act remain unexpended or unencumbered after June 1, 2033, the amount

1 (i) The name of the grantee or the description of the project, provided

6 the identity of the grantee can be determined, and when the difference in the description of

10 with the State of Maryland and recorded with the Board of Public Works. In all other

17 with the public purpose of the appropriation.
18 (c) (i) The Office of Policy Analysis shall have 45 days to review and
19 comment on the proposed use of the funds.
20 (ii) If the Office of Policy Analysis does not submit written objections
21 within 45 days, the Department of Budget and Management shall provide certification in
22 writing to the Board of Public Works that the proposed use of funds may be approved
23 notwithstanding technical differences in the appropriation in Section 1(3) Items ZA00
24 through ZB02 of this Act.
25 (d) It is the intent of the General Assembly that the provisions of this
26 paragraph:
27 (i) Provide an administrative process authorizing the approval of
28 grants by the Board of Public Works, provided that the proposed use of funds is consistent
29 with the public purpose of the original appropriation; and
30 (ii) Be applicable to this Act and all prior Maryland Consolidated
31 Capital Bond Loans.

12 SECTION 3. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That the General Assembly
13 declares that it is the public policy of this State to manage State general obligation bond
14 debt in a manner that will maintain Maryland’s high quality credit rating. The General
15 Assembly further declares that legislative oversight, control, and review of all forms of
16 State obligations are essential to maintenance of the State’s existing bond rating and
17 protection of the fiscal integrity of the State.
18 SECTION 4. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, before work may commence
19 pursuant to any supplement to any appropriation contained in this Act, satisfactory
20 evidence must be given to the Board of Public Works that the project can be completed with
21 the aggregate of the funds in this Act and previously appropriated for the stated purpose.
22 SECTION 5. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
23 (1) with the approval of the Department of Budget and Management, any
24 appropriation for design provided in this Act may be used to fund construction if the amount
25 of the appropriation exceeds the amount required for design expenses, including allowances
26 for contingencies; and
27 (2) with the approval of the Department of Budget and Management, any
28 appropriation for construction provided in this Act may be used to purchase capital
29 equipment if the amount of the appropriation exceeds the amount required for construction
30 expenses, including allowances for contingencies.
31 SECTION 6. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, except as otherwise provided
32 in this Act, before a State agency or institution named in this Act as responsible for an
33 individual item may begin work with funds appropriated by this Act, the agency or
34 institution shall provide satisfactory evidence to the Board of Public Works that the work
35 described in the individual item can be completed with the funds specified for that item.
36 SECTION 7. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, with the approval of the
37 Department of Budget and Management, any appropriation under the provisions of this
38 Act that is in excess of the amount needed for a project may be credited to the Construction
39 Contingency Fund under § 3–609 of the State Finance and Procurement Article.

1 Notwithstanding the fund balance restriction set forth in § 3–609(c) of the State Finance
2 and Procurement Article, any funds credited to the Fund may cause the total balance in
3 the Fund to exceed 1.25% of the capital debt affordability limit as determined under Title
4 8 of the State Finance and Procurement Article, in fiscal year 2027.
5 SECTION 8. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That, if federal funds are available
6 to help accomplish any project identified in this Act, the State agency or institution
7 responsible for the project shall make efforts through proper administrative procedures to
8 obtain these federal funds. Before spending any funds appropriated by this Act, the agency
9 or institution shall certify its efforts to the Board of Public Works and state the reason for
10 any failure to obtain federal funds. If federal funds are obtained, they shall be used to defray
11 the costs of the project described in this Act and not to expand its scope.
12 SECTION 9. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That:
13 (1) for any appropriation for the planning of a State–owned project provided in
14 this Act, if a program required by § 3–602(d) of the State Finance and Procurement Article
15 has not been submitted, the State agency or institution responsible for the project shall
16 submit a program to the Department of Budget and Management for approval before funds
17 may be expended from the appropriation; and
18 (2) for any appropriation for the construction of a State–owned project provided
19 in this Act, if preliminary plans and outline specifications required by § 3–602(f)(2)(i) of the
20 State Finance and Procurement Article have not been prepared, the State agency or
21 institution responsible for the project shall submit preliminary plans and outline
22 specifications to the Department of Budget and Management for approval before funds may
23 be expended from the appropriation.
24 SECTION 10. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That no portion of the proceeds of
25 a loan or any of the matching funds provided for a project funded under this Act may be
26 used for the furtherance of an essentially religious endeavor. Upon the request of the Board
27 of Public Works, a recipient of the proceeds of a loan under this Act shall submit evidence
28 satisfactory to the Board that none of the proceeds of the loan or any matching funds have
29 been or are being used for a purpose prohibited by this Act.
30 SECTION 11. AND BE IT FURTHER ENACTED, That the Comptroller may
31 advance funds to any loan funds account established pursuant to a general obligation bond
32 loan enabling Act for any expenditure authorized by that Act, provided that if general
33 obligation bonds have not been issued under the authority of that Act, the next ensuing
34 sale of general obligation bonds shall include the issuance of bonds under the authority of
35 that Act in an amount at least equivalent to the amount of the funds so advanced.
